011                                                 A BSTRACT
012
013              Highly performant large-scale pre-trained models promise to also provide a valuable
014              foundation for learning specialized tasks, by fine-tuning the model to the desired
015              task. By starting from a good general-purpose model, the goal is to achieve both
016
                 specialization in the target task and maintain robustness. To assess the robustness
                 of models to out-of-distribution samples after fine-tuning on downstream datasets,
017
                 we introduce a new robust fine-tuning benchmark, ImageNet-RIB (Robustness
018
                 Inheritance Benchmark). The benchmark consists of a set of related but distinct
019              specialized (downstream) tasks; pre-trained models are fine-tuned on one task in
020              the set and their robustness is assessed on the rest, iterating across all tasks for
021              fine-tuning and assessment. We find that the continual learning methods, EWC
022              and LwF maintain robustness after fine-tuning though fine-tuning generally does
023              reduce performance on generalization to related downstream tasks across models.
024              Not surprisingly, models pre-trained on large and rich datasets exhibit higher initial
025              robustness across datasets and suffer more pronounced degradation during fine-
026              tuning. The distance between the pre-training and downstream datasets, measured
027
                 by optimal transport, predicts this performance degradation on the pre-training
                 dataset. However, counterintuitively, model robustness after fine-tuning on related
028
                 downstream tasks is the worst when the pre-training dataset is the richest and the
029
                 most diverse. This suggests that starting with the strongest foundation model is not
030              necessarily the best approach for performance on specialist tasks. The benchmark
031              thus offers key insights for developing more resilient fine-tuning strategies and
032              building robust machine learning models1 .
033
034
035   1       I NTRODUCTION
036
037   Deep learning has progressed towards utilizing larger datasets (Lin et al., 2014; Russakovsky et al.,
038   2015; Schuhmann et al., 2022) and deeper architectures (Dosovitskiy et al., 2021; He et al., 2016;
039   Jiang et al., 2023). Consequently, starting with a model pre-trained on a large-scale dataset and
040   fine-tuning it for specific downstream tasks has become standard in machine learning to achieve
041
      better performance than training from scratch. While this approach capitalizes on the extensive
      knowledge embedded in pre-trained models, it often results in a significant loss of that knowledge
042
      due to catastrophic forgetting (French, 1999; Robins, 1995). To mitigate this issue, methods only
043
      training a part of the pre-trained model such as linear probing, low-rank adaptation (Hu et al., 2021),
044   and visual prompt (Bahng et al., 2022) have been proposed. However, these methods typically
045   underperform compared to fine-tuning the entire model on the downstream task.
046
047
      Fine-tuning on the downstream task also negatively impacts a model’s robustness to out-of-distribution
      (OOD) samples as the model is optimized for a narrower distribution (Figure 1). This issue has been
048
      extensively studied using various OOD datasets, typically beginning with an ImageNet pre-trained
049
      model and evaluating it on OOD datasets that exhibit natural distribution shifts, such as changes in
050   viewpoints (Barbu et al., 2019), time (Recht et al., 2019), styles (Hendrycks et al., 2021a; Wang et al.,
051   2019), or synthetic data based on the original dataset (Hendrycks & Dietterich, 2019; Salvador &
052   Oberman, 2022).
053

              https://jd730.github.io/projects/ImageNet-RIB

      Figure 1: Conceptual diagram of the impact of fine-tuning on pre-trained models on out-of-
066
      distribution (OOD) generalization. A model fpre pre-trained on the dataset Dpre (purple solid
067
      circle) can generalize to certain out-of-distribution data (purple dashed circle). The dashed gray line
068   represents a volume (D) containing inter-related OOD datasets (dark gray ellipsoids). Fine-tuning on
069   one of these datasets, referred to as the downstream dataset (Ddown , blue) shifts fpre to fdown , making
070   it more specialized to Ddown (blue dashed ellipsoid). This specialization improves performance on
071   Ddown and possibly others within the inter-related OOD set (green solid ellipsoids), but may also lead
072   to degradation on some OOD datasets (red solid ellipsoids).
073   Taori et al. (2020) proposed a benchmark that evaluates pre-trained models fine-tuned on ImageNet-
074   1K across multiple realistic ImageNet-based OOD datasets. It is widely used to measure model
075   robustness changes after fine-tuning (Kumar et al., 2022; Wortsman et al., 2022a;b) However, this
076   benchmark only uses one downstream task (ImageNet-1K), and certain pre-training datasets may
077
      include parts of ImageNet as they are often uncurated (Schuhmann et al., 2022). This limitation
      motivates the need for a broader and more comprehensive evaluation of robustness across multiple
078
      OOD datasets.
079
080   In this paper, we introduce ImageNet-RIB (Robustness Inheritance Benchmark), a new benchmark
081   designed to assess the robustness of fine-tuned models across diverse downstream and evaluation
082   OOD dataset pairs related to ImageNet. For each experiment, we fine-tune a pre-trained model on
083
      one OOD dataset (as a downstream dataset) and evaluate its performance on the remaining OOD
      datasets. This process is repeated across all available datasets to thoroughly assess how well the
084
      model retains robustness after fine-tuning. To achieve this, we employ a variety of fine-tuning
085
      strategies, including vanilla fine-tuning, linear probing (fine-tuning the last layer only), LoRA (Hu
086   et al., 2021), regularization-based continual learning methods (Li & Hoiem, 2017; Zenke et al., 2017),
087   and robust fine-tuning methods (Kumar et al., 2022; Wortsman et al., 2022a;b). We also investigate
088   the relationship between dataset distance metrics and robust fine-tuning outcomes, allowing us to
089   estimate the robustness changes prior to training.
090
      Our experimental results show that models pre-trained on larger and more diverse datasets demonstrate
091
      superior robustness on the OOD datasets and accuracy on ImageNet-1K. However, fine-tuning causes
092   performance drops on ImageNet-1K, which we find is aligned with the distance between the pre-
093   training dataset and the downstream dataset, as measured by Optimal Transport Dataset Distance
094   (OTDD) (Alvarez-Melis & Fusi, 2020). The combination of Model Soup (Wortsman et al., 2022a)
095   with regularization-based continual learning methods achieves the best performance in the benchmark,
096   while linear probing performs the best when using LAION-2B pre-trained models. Furthermore, our
097   findings indicate that continual learning methods not only mitigate catastrophic forgetting related
098   to the pre-training dataset but also enhance robustness when compared to standard fine-tuning.
099   This improvement is attributed to leveraging the distributional properties of both pre-training and
100
      downstream datasets. Interestingly, pre-training on LAION-2B, despite its size and diversity, does
      not always yield the best results when fine-tuned on downstream tasks, suggesting that starting with
101
      large, rich datasets may not always be the optimal approach for preserving robustness.
102
103   In summary, the contributions of this paper are four-fold:
104
105          • We propose ImageNet-RIB, a new benchmark leveraging multiple ImageNet-based OOD
106
               datasets to quantify the robustness of fine-tuned models in comparison to pre-trained models.
107          • We find that the performance drop on the pre-training dataset during fine-tuning can be
               predicted by the distance between pre-training and downstream datasets.


                                                             2
      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


108
             • We empirically demonstrate that regularization-based continual learning methods improve
109            robustness by leveraging both the pre-training and downstream dataset distributions and this
110            improvement is amplified when combined with robust fine-tuning methods.
111
112          • The absolute performance of the models pre-trained on richer datasets is worse on the
113            downstream tasks, suggesting that starting with rich foundation models may not always be
114            the best approach.
115
116
117
      2     R ELATED W ORK
118
119
120   2.1   ROBUSTNESS IN M ACHINE L EARNING
121
122   Robustness in machine learning refers to a model’s ability to maintain performance under various
123   perturbations, such as noise, corruption, and domain shifts. Robustness is typically evaluated on
124   synthetic datasets derived from original data (Hendrycks & Dietterich, 2019; Salvador & Oberman,
125
      2022) or real-world datasets featuring distribution shifts, such as different viewpoints (Barbu et al.,
      2019), styles (Hendrycks et al., 2021a; Wang et al., 2019), or temporal changes (Recht et al., 2019).
126
      To develop more robust models, data augmentation techniques have been widely explored including
127
      style transfer (Geirhos et al., 2019), perturbation-based image-to-image networks (Hendrycks et al.,
128   2021a), and adversarial logit pairing (Kannan et al., 2018). Robust-fine-tuning usually aims to
129   maintain the robustness of the pre-trained model to OOD datasets during fine-tuning. Taori et al.
130   (2020) address the limitations of previous robustness evaluations that used synthetic datasets by
131   proposing a new evaluation protocol that utilizes realistic datasets; ImageNet-V2, ImageNet-A,
132   ImageNet-R, ImageNet-Sketch, and ObjectNet after fine-tuning on ImageNet. This benchmark
133   is widely used with vision and language models such as CLIP (Radford et al., 2021). Shi et al.
134   (2023) extend this to joint training on two dataset; ImageNet-1K with CIFAR-10 (Krizhevsky et al.,
135   2009) or YFCC (Thomee et al., 2016). To solve this problem, Wortsman et al. (2022a) demonstrate
136
      that averaging the parameters of multiple trained models improves both in-distribution and OOD
      performance. WiSE-FT (Wortsman et al., 2022b) further shows that linearly interpolating the weights
137
      of pre-trained CLIP and ImageNet fine-tuned CLIP improves robustness, although it requires tuning
138
      the interpolation ratio for optimal performance. Goyal et al. (2023) show that contrastive learning
139   using text encoder in fine-tuning improves robustness. Kumar et al. (2022) propose a two-stage
140   method (LP-FT) that first applies linear probing followed by fine-tuning the entire network. Recently
141   concurrent work (Ramanujan et al., 2024) analyzes the effect of pre-training datasets on robust
142   fine-tuning in the WILDS (Koh et al., 2021) dataset, showing that having more data is beneficial,
143   while greater diversity per class is not. Unlike existing benchmarks (Shi et al., 2023; Taori et al.,
144   2020), which only fine-tune on ImageNet or two datasets simultaneously from unknown or uncurated
145   pre-training datasets, our benchmark provides diverse downstream datasets for a comprehensive
146   understanding of robust fine-tuning.
147
148
149   2.2   S INGLE D OMAIN G ENERALIZATION
150
151   Single-domain generalization refers to the task where only one source domain is available during
152   training, and the model is evaluated on multiple unseen target domains (Qiao et al., 2020). While the
153
      high-level concept is similar to the existing robust fine-tuning benchmark (Taori et al., 2020), the
      objectives differ. Robust fine-tuning focuses on maintaining or improving a model’s robustness to
154
      OOD datasets during fine-tuning, whereas single-domain generalization aims to achieve generalization
155
      to unseen OOD datasets, often through meta-learning-based data augmentation (Chen et al., 2023;
156   Qiao et al., 2020) or adaptive batch normalization (Fan et al., 2021). Recently, Fan et al. (2021)
157   applied single-domain generalization to the PACS dataset (Li et al., 2017), using one domain as
158   the training set and the remaining domains as test sets. This setup resembles our ImageNet-RIB
159   benchmark in that each dataset is used for training while the others are used for testing. However, the
160   goals of the two benchmarks differ: our robust fine-tuning benchmark aims to mitigate robustness
161   degradation during fine-tuning, while single-domain generalization benchmarks focus on improving
      generalizability from a single source domain.

178   dataset from the set of ImageNet OOD datasets as the downstream dataset Ddown (2) The pre-trained
179   model is fine-tuned on Ddown , then (3) evaluated on the remaining OOD datasets to assess robustness

181   downstream tasks, ensuring a detailed evaluation of fine-tuning’s impact on robustness.
182
183
184   2.3     C ONTINUAL L EARNING
185
186   Continual learning aims to enable models to learn new tasks without forgetting previously learned
187
      knowledge. Existing approaches can be broadly categorized into three types: regularization-based
      methods, replay-based methods, and architecture-based methods. Regularization-based methods (Che-
188
      ung et al., 2019; Kirkpatrick et al., 2017; Li & Hoiem, 2017; Zenke et al., 2017) use additional loss
189
      terms to limit changes to the model’s parameters, ensuring that previously learned knowledge is
190   retained. For instance, Kirkpatrick et al. (2017) employ the Fisher information matrix to determine
191   the importance of each parameter, helping to preserve critical weights from earlier tasks. Li & Hoiem
192   (2017) use knowledge distillation to transfer outputs from a model trained on past tasks to guide
193   learning new tasks. Replay-based methods (Robins, 1995) mitigate catastrophic forgetting by creating
194   a replay buffer that contains a small subset of previous task data or synthetic data (Van de Ven et al.,
195   2020) and a model is trained on the buffer along with a new task. Techniques such as reservoir
196   sampling, reinforcement learning (Rebuffi et al., 2017), and gradient-based selection (Aljundi et al.,
197   2019) help efficiently manage memory and select important data. Architecture-based methods modify
198
      the model’s structure to accommodate new tasks. These methods dynamically grow the network as
      needed. For example, Rusu et al. (2016), Yan et al. (2021), and Wang et al. (2022) introduce new
199
      model components for each task and use distillation to integrate them with the previous model. In our
200
      work, we focus on regularization-based continual learning methods to ensure a fair comparison with
201   other fine-tuning approaches.
202
203
204   3     I MAGE N ET ROBUSTNESS I NHERITANCE B ENCHMARK (I MAGE N ET-RIB)
205
206   We propose the ImageNet-RIB (Robustness Inheritance Benchmark), a novel benchmark designed
207   to measure robustness using existing ImageNet-related out-of-distribution (OOD) datasets as both
208   downstream and evaluation datasets. ImageNet-RIB fine-tunes pre-trained models on a variety of
209   downstream datasets, then evaluates robustness to other OOD datasets in the benchmark (Figure 2),
210   offering a more comprehensive understanding of robustness fine-tuning.
211
212   3.1     B ENCHMARK P ROTOCOL AND ROBUSTNESS M ETRIC
213
214   Protocol Figure 2 and Algorithm 1 in Appendix illustrate the protocol of our benchmark. Given a
215   set of out-of-distribution (OOD) datasets D = {D1 , D2 , ..., Dn }, a model pre-trained on the dataset
      Dpre is fine-tuned on the downstream dataset Ddown ∼ D. After fine-tuning, both the pre-trained


                                                                          4
      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


216
      model and the fine-tuned model are evaluated on the remaining datasets in D \ Ddown . This process is
217   repeated by selecting each dataset in D as the downstream dataset.
218
219   Metric We define the robustness improvement score (RI) as the average relative robustness (Taori
220   et al., 2020). Specifically, RI measures the accuracy difference between fine-tuned and pre-trained
221   models on OOD datasets. Formally, robustness improvement (RI) after fine-tuning on Di (= Ddown )
222   is defined as:
                                                        n
223                                              1     X       (j)
                                        RIi =                Ai − A(j)pre ,                            (1)
224                                            n−1
                                                         j=1,j̸=i
225
             (j)      (j)
226   where Apre and Ai denote the average accuracies of pre-trained and fine-tuned models on Dj ,
227   respectively. In addition to relative robustness, effective robustness (Taori et al., 2020) is an alternative
228   metric commonly used to evaluate OOD performance. Effective robustness measures how much the
229   accuracy of a model deviates from an expected baseline, typically using a reference in-distribution
230
      dataset (e.g., ImageNet-1K). While effective robustness is insightful, we use relative robustness in
      this benchmark to facilitate direct comparisons between different fine-tuning methods and initial
231
      pre-training datasets. We summarize the overall robustness improvement across all datasets as the
232
      mean robustness improvement (mRI).
233
234
      3.2   DATASET S UITES
235
236   We leverage all existing ImageNet OOD datasets designed for measuring robustness to distribu-
237   tion shifts: ImageNet-V2 (Recht et al., 2019), ImageNet-A (Hendrycks et al., 2021b), ImageNet-
238   Drawing (Salvador & Oberman, 2022), ImageNet-Cartoon (Salvador & Oberman, 2022), and
239   ImageNet-Sketch (Wang et al., 2019), ObjectNet (Barbu et al., 2019), and ImageNet-C (Hendrycks &
240   Dietterich, 2019). Although ObjectNet and ImageNet-C were originally designed solely for evaluat-
241   ing the OOD performance of ImageNet pre-trained models, with restrictions on their use for training,
242   we extend their application in this benchmark by fine-tuning models on these datasets and evaluating
243
      their robustness on other OOD datasets. For detailed descriptions of each dataset, please refer to
      Appendix A.1.
244
245
246   4     E XPERIMENTS
247
248   We use the RIB benchmark to assess the robustness of different pre-trained models to fine-tune on a
249   set of related downstream tasks. The goal is to assess which methods of fine-tuning do best across
250   multiple pre-training datasets.
251
252   4.1   E XPERIMENTAL D ETAILS
253
      Pre-Trained Models We use several architectures of Vision Transformer (ViT) (Dosovitskiy et al.,
254
      2021) and ResNet (He et al., 2016). The models are pre-trained on ImageNet-1K (Russakovsky et al.,
255
      2015), or ImageNet-21K (Ridnik et al., 2021) and then fine-tuned on ImageNet-1K. The standard
256   data augmentation and regularization technique for ViT, AugReg (Steiner et al., 2022) can also be
257   used for training on ImageNet-1K or ImageNet-21K. Alternatively, some models are pre-trained on
258   LAION-2B (Schuhmann et al., 2022) or OpenAI CLIP (Radford et al., 2021), followed by fine-tuning
259   on ImageNet-1K. In other words, all pre-trained models are trained on ImageNet-1K to directly
260   leverage its classifier before conducting experiments. For simplicity, we refer to them by the names
261   of the first pre-training datasets (e.g., ImageNet-21K, LAION-2B).
262   In the main paper, we focus on ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained ViT-B/16 and experiments
263   using other pre-trained models are reported in Appendix D along with ImageNet-1K with SAM (Chen
264   et al., 2022) and ImageNet-21K-P (Ridnik et al., 2021). We employ the timm (Wightman, 2019) and
265   torchvision (maintainers & contributors, 2016) for acquiring model weights and implementation.
266   Please refer to Appendix A.2 for more details.
267
268   Methods We employ standard fine-tuning methods, regularization-based continual learning meth-
269   ods, and robust fine-tuning methods for measuring performance on the proposed benchmark. The
      fine-tuning methods we evaluate include vanilla fine-tuning (FT), Linear Probing, LoRA (Hu et al.,

      to reveal the source of the parameters.
308
309
310
      Training Each pre-trained model is fine-tuned on the downstream dataset for 10 epochs with a
      batch size of 64. We use stochastic gradient descent (SGD) with a learning rate of 0.005 and a
311
      momentum of 0.9 with cosine annealing (Loshchilov & Hutter, 2017). Visual Prompt is trained
312
      for 10 epochs with a learning rate of 40 without weight decay following Bahng et al. (2022). The
313   experiment was conducted on NVIDIA A100. Please refer to Appendix A.3 and the code repository
314   for detailed implementation.
315
316
      Dataset Distance We measure the distance between datasets by using Optimal Transport Dataset
317   Distance (OTDD) (Alvarez-Melis & Fusi, 2020) and Normalized Compression Distance (NCD) (Cili-
318   brasi & Vitányi, 2005). We measure the distance in the image space and the feature space from
319   ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained ViT-16/B, class tokens before the classifier layer. For NCD,
320   we employ concatenated images and features. We use OTDD in the feature space in the main paper
321   and other distance metrics are discussed in Appendix B.
322
          2
323         We do not use other continual learning methods as the pre-training dataset is not accessible, and to ensure a
      fair comparison with other methods.

345   4.2         O PTIMAL T RANSPORT DATASET D ISTANCE A LIGNS W ITH I MAGE N ET-1K ACCURACY
346               D ROP D URING F INE -T UNING
347
348
      First, we start with the baseline of assessing model performance on the set of OOD tasks without
      any fine-tuning. Not surprisingly, models pre-trained on larger and more diverse datasets have
349
      better performance on both ImageNet-1K and downstream datasets as shown in Table 1. However,
350
      the ImageNet-21K with AugReg pre-trained model achieves better performance on ImageNet-C
351   than LAION-2B pre-trained model since AugReg includes several corruptions in ImageNet-C (e.g.,
352   brightness and contrast).
353
354
      We consider how the accuracy on ImageNet-1K changes after fine-tuning on each downstream dataset.
      We compute the Optimal Transport Dataset Distance (OTDD) (Alvarez-Melis & Fusi, 2020) between
355
      downstream datasets and ImageNet-1K in the feature space extracted from pre-trained ViT-B/16
356
      models. Synthetic datasets are excluded from this comparison, as they are generated from the
357   ImageNet-1K validation set. In general, ImageNet-1K accuracy decreases as the distance between
358   the downstream dataset and ImageNet-1K (pre-training dataset) increases as shown in Figure 3. We
359   also calculate the Pearson correlation coefficient between the accuracy and the distance in Table 2
360   and there is a negative correlation regardless of the method except linear probing. Especially, FT and
361   Prompter show a strong correlation (< -0.5). However, we did not find clear evidence of a correlation
362   between the OTDD and the accuracy on out-of-distribution (OOD) datasets after fine-tuning on
363   downstream datasets. Please refer to Appendix B for comparison with other dataset distances.
364
365   4.3         M ODELS T HAT C OMBINE C ONTINUAL L EARNING WITH ROBUST F INE -T UNING D O B EST
366
367   Table 5 presents accuracy on each OOD dataset before and after fine-tuning an ImageNet-1K with
368   AugReg pre-trained ViT-B/16 model with each method on the downstream dataset. We also illustrate
369
      performance on each corruption in ImageNet-C in Table 34 in the Appendix. Linear probing (LP)
      generally changes performance on both ImageNet-1K and OOD datasets less than fine-tuning (FT)
370
      as the backbone network is fixed. However, both methods exhibit similar increase and decrease
371
      patterns. Visual Prompt reduces performance even on ImageNet-1K after fine-tuning on synthetic
372   datasets of the ImageNet validation set. This is inconsistent with Bahng et al. (2022), which showed
373   its robustness to OOD datasets. Continual learning methods and robust fine-tuning methods generally
374   improve performance on most OOD datasets after fine-tuning on the downstream datasets. A strong
375   correlation exists between ImageNet-R, ImageNet-Sketch, and ImageNet-Drawing, as they share
376   drawing and sketch renditions, and ImageNet-R and ImageNet-Sketch share images. Fine-tuning on
377   ImageNet-C improves performance on other synthetic datasets but the converse does not hold. This
      is because ImageNet-C contains 15 different corruptions with 5 different severity.


                                                                                                  7
      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025


378
      From these results, we see that the combination of a robust fine-tuning method (Wortsman et al.,
379   2022a) with continual learning methods (MS:PRE-FT-EWC-LwF) achieves the highest mean robust-
380   ness improvement (mRI) across different backbones and pre-training datasets as shown in Table 3.
381   Moreover, end-to-end continual learning methods show comparable performance to the multi-stage
382   method (Kumar et al., 2022) or the post-hoc robustness method (Wortsman et al., 2022b). We believe
383   that this shows the potential of continual learning methods in the field of robust fine-tuning. The
384   robustness of linear probing and Visual Prompt remains relatively unchanged since they do not modify
385   the models’ weights significantly but their performance on the downstream dataset tends to be worse
386   (see Appendix D.2). Consequently, they have much better performance with LAION-2B pre-trained
387
      models compared to other methods, which show a significant robustness decrease.
388   Individual robustness improvement scores (RI) after fine-tuning on each downstream dataset with
389   ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained ViT-B/16 also show that MS:PRE-FT-EWC-LwF consistently
390   performs the highest in most downstream datasets, followed by WiSE-FT as demonstrated in Table 4.
391   This is because they directly use the weights of pre-trained models, thus taking advantage of their
392   robustness. In contrast, Visual Prompt severely deteriorates robustness with all downstream datasets.
393
394   4.4   PARADOXICALLY, M ODELS P RE -T RAINED ON THE L ARGEST DATASETS D O W ORST
395         A FTER F INE -T UNING
396
      The extent of robustness degradation increases with the size and diversity of the pre-training dataset,
397
      as illustrated in Table 3 and Figure 4. As a result, the robustness of fine-tuned models pre-trained on
398   larger datasets (e.g., LAION-2B, OpenAI) exhibit worse robustness compared to those pre-trained
399   on smaller datasets and their corresponding fine-tuned counterparts when using vanilla fine-tuning.
400   One possible explanation is that models pre-trained on the larger, more diverse dataset demonstrate
401   higher robustness to OOD datasets (see Table 1). Consequently, these models have more room
402   for performance degradation from catastrophic forgetting. However, this does not fully explain
403   the pronounced robustness loss observed in LAION-2B pre-trained models and OpenAI CLIPs,
404   particularly when compared to ImageNet-21K with AugReg pre-trained models, which exhibit similar
405   initial robustness. Moreover, Appendix C shows that these models learn downstream datasets slower
406
      than the ImageNet-21K with AugReg pre-trained model and the catastrophic robustness degradation
      happens in the beginning of fine-tuning.
407
408   Notably, ImageNet-21K and its variants begin to cause robustness degradation, especially when
409   using vanilla fine-tuning. This could be an early indicator of performance decay in larger pre-trained
410   models. Although ImageNet-21K is the second-largest dataset with 14 million images, it is much
411   smaller than LAION-2B, which contains two billion images. We hypothesize that this discrepancy in
412
      dataset size contributes to the difference in robustness degradation. However, further investigation is
      required to pinpoint when severe robustness degradation begins and to identify its underlying causes.
413
414
415   5     D ISCUSSION
416
417   In this work, we introduced ImageNet-RIB (Robustness Inheritance Benchmark), a comprehensive
418   benchmark designed to assess the robustness of fine-tuned models relative to pre-trained models across
419   diverse out-of-distribution (OOD) datasets. A key distinction of ImageNet-RIB is that it fine-tunes
420   models on multiple downstream datasets and evaluates their performance on various OOD datasets,
421   providing a more holistic understanding of robustness compared to the prior benchmark (Taori et al.,
422
      2020), which focused on a single downstream dataset. This expanded framework allows us to better
      examine how downstream dataset distributions affect OOD performance.
423
424   Our results demonstrate that continual learning methods and robust fine-tuning approaches, partic-
425   ularly in combination, are effective in preserving or even improving robustness. Specifically, the
426   combination of Model Soup with continual learning techniques consistently achieved superior perfor-
427   mance. This finding underscores the potential of integrating these strategies to mitigate catastrophic
428
      forgetting and enhance the robustness to OOD datasets.
429   We also found that models pre-trained on larger, more diverse datasets, such as LAION-2B, experi-
430   enced more severe robustness degradation during fine-tuning. While these models exhibited high
431   initial robustness, the performance drop was more prominent compared to models pre-trained on
      smaller datasets like ImageNet-1K, leading to even worse performance. In these scenarios, simpler

458   Figure 4: Fine-tuning LAION-2B pre-trained model and OpenAI CLIP cause severe robustness
459   loss relative to ImageNet-1K pre-trained model. The average accuracy on OOD datasets before
460   (blue) and after (red) fine-tuning with each method on downstream datasets. The red bar is calculated
461   directly by evaluating pre-trained models on OOD datasets while the blue bar is calculated by adding
462   mRI of each method to the pre-trained models’ accuracy. Note that it is identical to the average
                                                                                               Pn (i)
463   accuracy on OOD datasets after fine-tuning on each downstream dataset (mRI + n1 i Apre =
       1
         P     1
                  P  n       (i)
464
      n    j n−1     i,i̸=j Adown ). Fine-tuning LAION-2B pre-trained model and OpenAI CLIP on the
465   downstream OOD datasets causes severe robustness loss leading to worse performance than ImageNet-
466   1K with AugReg pre-trained model. Conversely, ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained model
467   improves robustness after fine-tuning. Note that the difference between red and blue bars is mRI.
468
469   methods such as linear probing, which freeze most of the model’s layers, were more effective in
470   maintaining robustness, as more complex methods often led to significant performance degradation.
471   This highlights the nuanced relationship between the size and diversity of the pre-training dataset and
472   the model’s ability to generalize after fine-tuning.
473
      Despite these contributions, our work has certain limitations. We primarily focused on fine-tuning,
474   continual learning, and robust fine-tuning methods. Future research could explore the role of advanced
475   data augmentation techniques (Cubuk et al., 2019; Hendrycks et al., 2021a; Wang et al., 2023) in
476   further improving OOD robustness. Moreover, while Optimal Transport Dataset Distance (OTDD)
477   shows promise in predicting performance degradation on the pre-training dataset after fine-tuning,
478   more refined metrics are needed to better capture and address robustness degradation.
479
      Future research should focus on understanding the significant robustness degradation after fine-tuning
480   observed in models pre-trained on larger datasets like LAION-2B. Uncovering why such extensive
481   pre-training leads to worse robustness compared to models pre-trained on smaller datasets could
482   inform more effective robustness fine-tuning strategies. Moreover, expanding the scope of our
483   analysis to include a broader range of model architectures and datasets would further enhance the
484   generalizability of our findings. We believe that ImageNet-RIB offers a valuable framework for
485   studying the impact of fine-tuning on OOD generalization, and we hope this work encourages further
      research into developing more robust and generalizable machine learning models.

702
      Algorithm 1 Protocol of ImageNet-RIB
703
704   Input: A set of out-of-distribution datasets D = {D1 , D2 , ..., Dn }, pre-trained model fpre , fine-
705
          tuning method fine-tune(·).
      Output: Mean robustness improvement, mRI.
706
       1: procedure I MAGE N ET-RIB
707
       2:     for Ddown (= Di ) ∈ D do
708    3:         fdown ← fine-tune(fpre ; Ddown )       ▷ Fine-tune pre-trained model fpre on Ddown .
709    4:         for Dj ∈ D \ Ddown do
710                     (j)
       5:             Ai = eval(fdown ; Dj )                                      ▷ Evaluate fdown on Dj .
711                     (j)
712
       6:             Apre = eval(fpre ; Dj )                                       ▷ Evaluate fpre on Dj .
       7:         end for
713                         1
                              Pn           (j)     (j)
       8:         RIi = n−1     j=1,j̸=i Ai − Apre          ▷ Calculate Robustness Improvement (RI).
714
       9:     end for P
715                       n
      10:     mRI = i RIi                                                            ▷ Calculate mean RI.
716   11: end procedure
717
718
719   A PPENDIX
720
721
      A     E XPERIMENTAL D ETAILS
722
723   In this section, we describe the details of the experimental setup.
724
725
      A.1   O UT- OF -D ISTRIBUTION DATASETS IN I MAGE N ET-RIB
726
727
728
      We leverage all existing ImageNet variants designed to measure the robustness of the trained network
729
      during distribution shifts. ImageNet-O (Hendrycks et al., 2021b) is not used since it is an out-of-
730   distribution detection dataset.
731
732   ImageNet-V2 (Recht et al., 2019) ImageNet-V2 is designed to have a distribution as similar as
733   possible to the original ImageNet-1K. It has 50,000 images with 1,000 classes same as the original
734   validation set. The dataset is used under the MIT license.
735
736   ImageNet-A (Hendrycks et al., 2021b) ImageNet-A is an adversarially filtered test image that
737   ImageNet-1K pre-trained ResNet-50 (He et al., 2016) is difficult to predict correctly. It contains 7,500
738   images with 200 difficult subclasses from ImageNet-1K. The dataset is used under the MIT license.
739
740   ImageNet-R (Hendrycks et al., 2021a) ImageNet-R (Renditions) contains 30,000 images from
741   200 ImageNet classes with various rendition styles such as painting, sculpture, embroidery, origami,
742   cartoon, toy, and so on. The drawing rendition overlaps with ImageNet-Sketch (Wang et al., 2019).
743
      The dataset is used under the MIT license.
744
      ImageNet-Sketch (Wang et al., 2019) ImageNet-Sketch comprises black and white sketch draw-
745
      ings of the ImageNet-1K classes and each class has 50 images. The dataset is used under the MIT
746
      license.
747
748   ImageNet-Cartoon and ImageNet-Drawing (Salvador & Oberman, 2022) ImageNet-Cartoon
749   and ImageNet-Drawing are to be converted from ImageNet validation set images to cartoon, and
750   drawing styles based on generative adversarial network (Wang & Yu, 2020) and image processing (Lu
751   et al., 2012). These simplified representations test a model’s ability to identify objects from minimal-
752   istic and abstract visual information. The dataset is used under the Creative Commons Attribution 4.0
753   International license.
754
755   ObjectNet (Barbu et al., 2019) ObjectNet is designed for evaluating object recognition models
      under more realistic conditions such as various poses, backgrounds, and viewpoints. There are 50,000

      Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

771               ResNet-50         IN-1K         torchvision           ResNet50_Weights.DEFAULT
772
773
774   images with 313 object classes and 113 classes are overlapped with ImageNet. We only use ImageNet
775   class objects. The dataset is used under the MIT license.
776
777
      ImageNet-C (Hendrycks & Dietterich, 2019) ImageNet-C is designed for measuring the robust-
778
      ness of models to common perturbations such as noise, blur, weather, and digital distortions. In the
779
      dataset, ImageNet validation set images are perturbed with various severity from 1 to 5. Unlike the
780   original metrics, corruption error compared with AlexNet, we use average accuracy for consistency
781   with other datasets. The dataset is used under the Apache-2.0 license.
782
783
784
      A.2   P RE -T RAINED M ODEL
785
      Table 6 lists the libraries and corresponding network weight names for each model. We use the entire
786
      models in timm and torchvision library, which are finally fine-tuned on ImageNet-1K, with patch
787   sizes of 16 and 32, and input image shape of 224 among ViT small, base, and large. For ResNets, we
788   use the default ImageNet-1K pre-trained weights from the torchvision library.
789
790
791
792   A.3   T RAINING AND H YPERPARAMETERS
793
794   Each pre-trained model is fine-tuned on the downstream dataset for 10 epochs where the average
795   accuracy on downstream datasets for each pre-trained ViT-B/16 model achieves more than 90% with
796   vanilla fine-tuning. We applied LoRA on query and value projection layers with rank 8 following the
797
      original implementation (Hu et al., 2021). We use 2 as a temperature for calculating KL divergence for
      LwF following Li & Hoiem (2017). For WiSE-FT, we use the interpolation ratio between pre-trained
798
      and fine-tuned models as 0.5 following the recommendation by Wortsman et al. (2022b) instead of
799
      finding the best hyperparameters evaluated on the benchmark for the fair comparison.
800
801
802   B     DATASET D ISTANCE
803
804   We measure the Optimal Transport dataset distance(OTDD) (Alvarez-Melis & Fusi, 2020) between
805   each dataset using both images and the pre-trained model features from ImageNet-1K with AugReg
806   pre-trained ViT-B/16, as shown in Figures 5a and 5b, respectively. Since ImageNet-C comprises
807   multiple corruptions with different severities, we do not measure the distance to ImageNet-C. As
808   shown in Figure 5a, in the image space, ImageNet-Sketch is the farthest from other datasets as it is
809   black and white sketch images. ImageNet-Drawing is the closest to the dataset and the ImageNet-R
      is the second closest as they share the same styles and images, respectively.

835
836                    (c) NCD in the Image Space                                                                                        (d) NCD in the Feature Space
837
838   Figure 5: Optimal Transport Dataset Distances (OTDD) in the feature space aligns with each
839   dataset design. Pairwise OTDD (up) and Normalized Compression Distance (NCD) (down) between
840   datasets using images (left) and features extracted by ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained ViT-
841   B/16 on each dataset (right), respectively.
842
843
844   OTDD in the feature space (Figure 5b) demonstrates a better alignment with the dataset design
845   principles. For example, ImageNet-V2 is designed to replicate the distribution of the ImageNet
846   validation set. It leads ImageNet-V2 the closest to ImageNet-1K among realistic datasets. Moreover,
847   the distances between ImageNet-1K and ImageNet-V2 to other datasets are consistent across both
848   image and feature spaces. This is not true with ImageNet-Cartoon since it is a synthetic dataset based
849
      on the ImageNet validation set. As shown in Table 5, ImageNet-Cartoon improves ImageNet-1K
      accuracy more than ImageNet-Drawing, suggesting that the distribution shift in cartoon-style images
850
      is less severe than that of drawing-style images. Similarly, ObjectNet is intentionally collected with
851
      different viewpoints and backgrounds and it is the most distant from all other datasets in the feature
852   space.
853
854   We also measure Normalized Compression Distance (NCD) using both images and the features from
855
      ImageNet-1K with AugReg pre-trained ViT-B/16. However, the distance between each dataset pair is
      too insignificant to compare with each dataset as shown in Figures 5c and 5d.
856

      earlier compared to other models. To investigate this, we analyze the robustness performance change

      Figure 6: Fine-tuning LAION-2B and OpenAI pre-trained model cause severe robustness loss

      more rapidly than other methods, while the OpenAI CLIP models exhibit the slowest learning pace.

894
      in robustness to out-of-distribution datasets. This suggests that overfitting is not the primary cause of

      the dramatic performance decline.

910
      performance.

938   Across the ImageNet pre-trained models, WiSE-FT and Model Soup consistently have better robust-
939   ness improvement compared to other methods fine-tuning on realistic OOD datasets (Tables 11, 13,
940   and 14). Linear Probing consistently achieves the best robustness improvement using LAION-2B
941   pre-trained models (Table 16) and OpenAI CLIP models (Table 17).
